[30;1m363 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m364 | [0m[35mNormally `qs.update(...)` doesn't emit any events and thus doesn't trigger invalidation.[0m
[30;1m365 | [0m[35mAnd there is no transparent and efficient way to do that: trying to act on conditions will[0m

[30;1m367 | [0m[35mand to act on specific objects we will need to fetch all of them,[0m
[30;1m368 | [0m[35mwhich `QuerySet.update()` users generally try to avoid.[0m

[30;1m20 | [0m[35m    Cacheops saves each DB resultset cache key in a "conj set" so it can delete it later if it[0m
[30;1m21 | [0m[35m    thinks it should be invalidated due to a saved record with matching values. But the resultset[0m
[30;1m22 | [0m[35m    caches time out after 30 minutes, and their cache keys live in those conj sets forever![0m
[30;1m23 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m24 | [0m[35m    So conj sets for frequent queries on tables that aren't updated often end up containing[0m
[30;1m25 | [0m[35m    millions of already-expired cache keys and maybe a few thousand actually useful ones,[0m
